When agreeing to exclude the supplier\u2019s liability for combination claims, it is generally acceptable to specify that: \u201cthe [Supplier] will have no liability for these combination claims for the portion of the obligation or liability determined on a fair and equitable basis to be attributable to a party other than the [Supplier] based on the materiality of the [Supplier products] to the combination claim\u201d.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 307, "text": "As for the carve-out on Zebracorp provided specifications, it is important to stress that the specifications have to be mandated by Zebracorp without any freedom of design for the supplier in order for the supplier to be able to shift the liability for IP infringement to Zebracorp. In most cases, Zebracorp will have to rely on the expertise of the supplier in building and designing the product, and the mere fact that Zebracorp provides certain requirements/specifications for the products it purchases should not transfer the risk of IP infringements over to Zebracorp.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 308, "text": "Another common carve-out proposed by sophisticated vendors seeks to exclude \u2018all claims asserted by a company, which exercises control over Zebracorp or which is controlled by Zebracorp\u2019. This carve out essentially prevents Zebracorp from taking advantage of the indemnity when the third party making the infringement claim is in fact not a third party but an affiliated company of Zebracorp. Such carve-outs are generally acceptable.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 309, "text": "The suppliers are fairly often likely to represent the viewpoint that Zebracorp should itself indemnify the supplier for any claims that are based on these carve-outs i.e. based on Zebracorp modifications etc. Such indemnities from Zebracorp to supplier should not be taken for granted. We should keep in mind that Zebracorp is not providing any products/services to the supplier against a fee and accordingly should not be expected to provide indemnities to the supplier. The indemnities should be provided by the selling party to the purchasing party.  Whenever the supplier is requesting an indemnity from Zebracorp it is worth asking the supplier whether the supplier would in fact be willing to indemnify Zebracorp in the event the supplier would provide products to Zebracorp free of charge.  That being said, agreeing to this type of indemnity is not out of the question. If worded carefully the indemnity can be used to limit Zebracorp\u2019s liability in cases where Zebracorp does cause a third party infringement claim by its own actions. Instead of agreeing to indemnity the supplier for all costs and damages, we should seek to only agree to defend the supplier against the third party claim.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 310, "text": "Entire Liability and Exclusive Remedies. It is fairly customary for the supplier to wish to expressly state that the indemnities and ancillary obligations agreed in the IP indemnity section of the agreement constitute the purchasing party\u2019s sole remedies and the supplier\u2019s sole liability. A typical clause introduced by the supplier could read in e.g. as follows: \u201cThis section contains i. the [Supplier]\u2019s entire liability and all obligations related to third party intellectual property infringement or misappropriation, and ii. the [Purchaser]\u2019s exclusive remedies against the [Supplier]  for such third party intellectual property infringement or misappropriation. These remedies are provided in lieu of all other warranties, whether express, implied or statutory\u201d. Such clauses are not problematic, and can be accepted so long as we have agreed on the supplier\u2019s liability for these IPR claims exclusively in the IP indemnity section of the agreement, which should practically always be the case.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 311, "text": "It is not uncommon for the seller to try to limit its liability for IPR infringement claims to any amounts that would have been due as a reasonable royalty based on the price of the seller\u2019s products.  The sellers include this limitation so as to ensure that they  end up paying royalties or license fees to a third party based on the value of their product as opposed to value of the Zebracorp product/solution. The difference between the two can be substantial as an example for a component supplier where the value of the infringing component is far lower than the value of in e.g. the Zebracorp system that incorporates the infringing component. Whilst the rationale behind such limitations is understandable, the effect of such limitation can put Zebracorp as substantial disadvantage, and these type of limitations should be carefully considered with IPR and/or Legal & Compliance.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 312, "text": "Zebracorp Preferred Position. --- CHUNK START ---
You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**
You may receive a `PREVIOUS CONTEXT` field. This tells you the state of the document immediately before the current chunk.
- If the previous chunk ended inside a section (e.g., "Table of Contents"), you MUST continue that section unless a clear new header appears.
- Do NOT start a new `CLAUSE_START` if the text is clearly a continuation of a list or table from the previous section.

**Style Rules:**
- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).
- Do NOT classify TOC items as `CLAUSE_START`.

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.
    - If the text says "Schedule", use `APPENDIX_START` (unless specifically instructed otherwise, but usually Schedule = Appendix).
- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:
    - If you are inside a section (e.g., Annex) and see text that looks like a table row (e.g., "| Col 1 | Col 2 |"), tag it as `CONTENT`.
    - **Ignore Repeated Headers**: If you see headers like "Table continued", "Page X", or repeated column names inside a table, tag them as `CONTENT`. Do NOT start a new section.

**Output Format:**
Return a JSON list of objects. Each object must have:
- `index`: The EXACT integer index from the input block.
- `type`: The classification tag.

Example: `[{"index": 0, "type": "INFO"}, {"index": 1, "type": "CLAUSE"}]`

**Allowed Tags & Rules:**

If Document Type is **MASTER** or **SUBORDINATE**:
**Goal:** Group the document into high-level sections. Do NOT split sub-sections.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-contractual section.
    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the first block (header/title) of this section.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

If Document Type is **REFERENCE**:
**Goal:** Identify Guidelines.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-guideline section.
    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).


CURRENT DOCUMENT TYPE: MASTER

**Allowed Tags:**

    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

If Document Type is **REFERENCE**:
**Goal:** Identify Guidelines.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-guideline section.
    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).

The term \u2018liability\u2019 in the context of a purchasing of products and/or services can be defined as an obligation on a party to pay damages or other monetary compensation by virtue of an act or omission attributable to that party. A limitation of liability (LoL) clause permits contracting parties to reduce or eliminate the potential for indirect and consequential and such other special type of damages should there be a breach of contract. In some cases, a liability cap on damages may be used. The rationale behind liability limitations is to allocate the risk between the manufacturer, distributor and end user.  For example, a defective resistor or capacitor might cost less than a dollar, but could cause millions of dollars in loss revenues and such other indirect damages if the defective component causes a system outage. For obvious reasons, sophisticated vendors will spend a lot of time and effort negotiating these LoL clauses.  Absent an agreement explicitly limiting a seller\u2019s liability, a seller is liable for indirect and consequential damages (including loss of profits, loss of revenue, and other damages which can still be reasonably foreseeable). The same applies to Zebracorp, as the purchasing party, which is why it is important to make sure that the LoL clause is mutual and applies also in favour of Zebracorp.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 350, "text": "Exclusion of Indirect Damages. Typical examples of indirect and consequential damages include loss of profit, loss of business, loss of revenue, loss of goodwill and loss of anticipated savings. The list can be expanded to include loss of business opportunity, lost sales or lost contracts. In contrast to indirect damages, direct damages are easily foreseeable and quantifiable. Examples of direct damages include the repair/replacement costs of a defective product, de-installation and reinstallation costs, transportation or storage costs and additional costs for expedited freight. Courts have not always been known to be uniform in their approach to determining whether an element of damages is \u201cdirect\u201d or \u201cindirect\u201d.  The governing law of the contract (Please see the section titled \u2018Governing Law\u2019 above for further details) will also play an important role as these concepts have varying interpretations in each country. Further guidance can be obtained by speaking to a member of the Legal & Compliance team.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 353, "text": "Many vendors seek to include \u2018cost of substitute goods\u2019 or \u2018cost of substitute procurement\u2019 into the list of indirect damages or to otherwise exclude all liability for cost of substitute procurement. Albeit somewhat unusual, the above can generally be accepted to be included into the list of indirect damages. --- CHUNK START ---
You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**
You may receive a `PREVIOUS CONTEXT` field. This tells you the state of the document immediately before the current chunk.
- If the previous chunk ended inside a section (e.g., "Table of Contents"), you MUST continue that section unless a clear new header appears.
- Do NOT start a new `CLAUSE_START` if the text is clearly a continuation of a list or table from the previous section.

**Style Rules:**
- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).
- Do NOT classify TOC items as `CLAUSE_START`.

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.
    - If the text says "Schedule", use `APPENDIX_START` (unless specifically instructed otherwise, but usually Schedule = Appendix).
- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:
    - If you are inside a section (e.g., Annex) and see text that looks like a table row (e.g., "| Col 1 | Col 2 |"), tag it as `CONTENT`.
    - **Ignore Repeated Headers**: If you see headers like "Table continued", "Page X", or repeated column names inside a table, tag them as `CONTENT`. Do NOT start a new section.

**Output Format:**
Return a JSON list of objects. Each object must have:
- `index`: The EXACT integer index from the input block.
- `type`: The classification tag.

Example: `[{"index": 0, "type": "INFO"}, {"index": 1, "type": "CLAUSE"}]`

**Allowed Tags & Rules:**

If Document Type is **MASTER** or **SUBORDINATE**:
**Goal:** Group the document into high-level sections. Do NOT split sub-sections.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-contractual section.
    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the first block (header/title) of this section.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

If Document Type is **REFERENCE**:
**Goal:** Identify Guidelines.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-guideline section.
    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).

This is because liabilities for damages in software contracts are typically substantial only in cases of third party IPR infringement claims. So the liability cap is really only relevant when facing a IPR infringement claim. Equally in hardware procurement contracts where product liability and IPR related claims are excluded from the monetary cap, the practical impact of the cap is often confined to liability for such systematic or epidemic failures that cause field retrofit or recall of installed products/equipment.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 366, "text": "It would also be important to note the difference between a maximum cap that applies to each incident, and a cap that applies for in e.g. each calendar year (as in the example above) and in e.g. an aggregate cap that applies for the entire duration of the contract no matter how many years the contract lasts and how many incidents occur during the term of the contract. In the latter case, a seemingly acceptable high number proposed by the supplier/subcontractor may prove to be inadequate if the same contract is used for several years. In many cases, it would be advisable to agree on a per incident cap or a per year cap instead of an aggregate cap for the entire duration of the contract.  If we go with the aggregate cap, it might be a good idea to agree on cap that is in e.g. 100 % (or some other acceptable percentage) of the value of the contract instead of a certain fixed dollar amount. --- CHUNK START ---
You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**
You may receive a `PREVIOUS CONTEXT` field. This tells you the state of the document immediately before the current chunk.
- If the previous chunk ended inside a section (e.g., "Table of Contents"), you MUST continue that section unless a clear new header appears.
- Do NOT start a new `CLAUSE_START` if the text is clearly a continuation of a list or table from the previous section.

**Style Rules:**
- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).
- Do NOT classify TOC items as `CLAUSE_START`.

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.
    - If the text says "Schedule", use `APPENDIX_START` (unless specifically instructed otherwise, but usually Schedule = Appendix).
- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:
    - If you are inside a section (e.g., Annex) and see text that looks like a table row (e.g., "| Col 1 | Col 2 |"), tag it as `CONTENT`.
    - **Ignore Repeated Headers**: If you see headers like "Table continued", "Page X", or repeated column names inside a table, tag them as `CONTENT`. Do NOT start a new section.

**Output Format:**
Return a JSON list of objects. Each object must have:
- `index`: The EXACT integer index from the input block.
- `type`: The classification tag.

Example: `[{"index": 0, "type": "INFO"}, {"index": 1, "type": "CLAUSE"}]`

**Allowed Tags & Rules:**

If Document Type is **MASTER** or **SUBORDINATE**:
**Goal:** Group the document into high-level sections. Do NOT split sub-sections.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-contractual section.
    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the first block (header/title) of this section.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

If Document Type is **REFERENCE**:
**Goal:** Identify Guidelines.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-guideline section.
    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).


CURRENT DOCUMENT TYPE: MASTER

--- CHUNK START ---
You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**
You may receive a `PREVIOUS CONTEXT` field. This tells you the state of the document immediately before the current chunk.
- If the previous chunk ended inside a section (e.g., "Table of Contents"), you MUST continue that section unless a clear new header appears.
- Do NOT start a new `CLAUSE_START` if the text is clearly a continuation of a list or table from the previous section.

**Style Rules:**
- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).
- Do NOT classify TOC items as `CLAUSE_START`.

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.
    - If the text says "Schedule", use `APPENDIX_START` (unless specifically instructed otherwise, but usually Schedule = Appendix).
- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:
    - If you are inside a section (e.g., Annex) and see text that looks like a table row (e.g., "| Col 1 | Col 2 |"), tag it as `CONTENT`.
    - **Ignore Repeated Headers**: If you see headers like "Table continued", "Page X", or repeated column names inside a table, tag them as `CONTENT`. Do NOT start a new section.

**Output Format:**
Return a JSON list of objects. Each object must have:
- `index`: The EXACT integer index from the input block.
- `type`: The classification tag.

Example: `[{"index": 0, "type": "INFO"}, {"index": 1, "type": "CLAUSE"}]`

**Allowed Tags & Rules:**

If Document Type is **MASTER** or **SUBORDINATE**:
**Goal:** Group the document into high-level sections. Do NOT split sub-sections.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-contractual section.
    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the first block (header/title) of this section.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

If Document Type is **REFERENCE**:
**Goal:** Identify Guidelines.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-guideline section.
    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).

--- CHUNK START ---
You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**
You may receive a `PREVIOUS CONTEXT` field. This tells you the state of the document immediately before the current chunk.
- If the previous chunk ended inside a section (e.g., "Table of Contents"), you MUST continue that section unless a clear new header appears.
- Do NOT start a new `CLAUSE_START` if the text is clearly a continuation of a list or table from the previous section.

**Style Rules:**
- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).
- Do NOT classify TOC items as `CLAUSE_START`.

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.
    - If the text says "Schedule", use `APPENDIX_START` (unless specifically instructed otherwise, but usually Schedule = Appendix).
- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:
    - If you are inside a section (e.g., Annex) and see text that looks like a table row (e.g., "| Col 1 | Col 2 |"), tag it as `CONTENT`.
    - **Ignore Repeated Headers**: If you see headers like "Table continued", "Page X", or repeated column names inside a table, tag them as `CONTENT`. Do NOT start a new section.

**Output Format:**

- `index`: The EXACT integer index from the input block.
- `type`: The classification tag.

**Allowed Tags & Rules:**

If Document Type is **MASTER** or **SUBORDINATE**:
**Goal:** Group the document into high-level sections. Do NOT split sub-sections.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-contractual section.
    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the first block (header/title) of this section.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**

**Critical Instructions:**

VAT is assessed and collected on the value of goods or services that have been provided every time there is a transaction (sale/purchase). The seller charges VAT to the buyer, and the seller pays this VAT to the government. If Zebracorp is the buyer, the tax we have paid for such purchases can be generally deducted from the tax we charge our customers. The burden of the tax is to a large extent passed onto the end consumer.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 483, "text": "Withholding Taxes. A withholding tax is generally any tax that is required to be withheld or deducted by the payer before making a payment. The party required to withhold or deduct the tax is required to pay the amount of the tax to the tax authorities instead of the beneficiary of the payment. The beneficiary of the payment should then be able to reclaim the withheld tax from its income tax, or in case the beneficiary has no income tax obligations, ask for a refund of the withheld tax. Governments use withholding tax as a means to secure payment of the taxes in particular when payments are made by an onshore buyer to an offshore seller. Sellers of goods and services are for obvious reasons often concerned about the effect of the withholding taxes as it reduces the amount of funds paid to them. Withholding taxes can become problematic when the seller is unable to obtain a corresponding tax credit or to recover the withheld amount from foreign tax authorities.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 484, "text": "More often than not sellers are keen to propose that the prices exclude withholding taxes. By stating this, the sellers are essentially saying that we should increase the amount of each invoice to the extent necessary to ensure that the seller receives and retain a net sum equal to the amount of the invoice without any withholding or deduction. Should we agree to this, not only would the prices payable by us increase by the amount of the withholding tax but we would also be paying the income tax of the seller. In most cases, it is not acceptable to exclude withholding tax from the prices. In exceptional cases, we can consider agreeing to gross-up the prices so that the supplier reserves the amount of money they would have received without the withholding tax. This can be the case when in e.g. we know that it is next to impossible for the supplier to reclaim or recover the withheld taxes. Before accepting to exclude withholding tax it is advisable to speak to Corporate Tax, so that we can properly assess the impact of the tax on the prices we pay.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 485, "text": "PRODUCT LIABILITY", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 486, "text": "General. A common example of a product liability claim is fire or explosion caused by defective equipment. The suppliers of products should keep Zebracorp fully indemnified against these type of injuries/damages. While the risk of such claim admittedly be relatively small, Zebracorp\u2019s potential liability associated with these type of incidents can be substantial, and any limitations on the supplier\u2019s liability whether in terms or maximum financial amount or otherwise should be carefully considered.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 487, "text": "We should not necessarily accept restricting the supplier\u2019s liability to claims made by third parties (i.e. other than Zebracorp) since Zebracorp may also be the injured party. This is in contrast to IPR indemnity where restricting the obligation to indemnity can be limited to third party claims only. We should also not accept to limit the supplier\u2019s liability to defects in either design or manufacturing of the products. The supplier of the defective product should assume responsibility irrespective of the root cause of the defect.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 488, "text": "Most countries have implemented mandatory product liability legislation that imposes strict liability on the manufacturer, importer or any retailer of the product. Under this strict liability, the manufacturer importer or any retailer is held liable if the product is defective, even if the manufacturer, importer or any retailer was not negligent in making that product defective. In contrast to strict liability, when the liability is limited to negligence the plaintiff must be able to prove that the defendant's conduct fell below the relevant standard of care. Our suppliers/subcontractors should also accept strict liability for any defects in the products that cause personal injury (including death) or damage to tangible or real property. This means that we should never accept to limit our suppliers/subcontractors\u2019 liability to damages caused by negligence or by their negligent acts.", "style": "Normal"}, {"index": 489, "text": "Vendors may seek to limit their indemnity/responsibility to any liability which is prescribed by applicable Product Liability legislation. The Product Liability legislation varies substantially from country to country and some jurisdictions may not have such legislation to begin with, and 2. You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**
You may receive a `PREVIOUS CONTEXT` field. This tells you the state of the document immediately before the current chunk.
- If the previous chunk ended inside a section (e.g., "Table of Contents"), you MUST continue that section unless a clear new header appears.
- Do NOT start a new `CLAUSE_START` if the text is clearly a continuation of a list or table from the previous section.

**Style Rules:**
- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).
- Do NOT classify TOC items as `CLAUSE_START`.

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.
    - If the text says "Schedule", use `APPENDIX_START` (unless specifically instructed otherwise, but usually Schedule = Appendix).
- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:
    - If you are inside a section (e.g., Annex) and see text that looks like a table row (e.g., "| Col 1 | Col 2 |"), tag it as `CONTENT`.
    - **Ignore Repeated Headers**: If you see headers like "Table continued", "Page X", or repeated column names inside a table, tag them as `CONTENT`. Do NOT start a new section.

**Output Format:**
Return a JSON list of objects. Each object must have:
- `index`: The EXACT integer index from the input block.
- `type`: The classification tag.

Example: `[{"index": 0, "type": "INFO"}, {"index": 1, "type": "CLAUSE"}]`

**Allowed Tags & Rules:**

If Document Type is **MASTER** or **SUBORDINATE**:
**Goal:** Group the document into high-level sections. Do NOT split sub-sections.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-contractual section.
    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the first block (header/title) of this section.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

If Document Type is **REFERENCE**:
**Goal:** Identify Guidelines.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-guideline section.
    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).


CURRENT DOCUMENT TYPE: MASTER

    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).

--- CHUNK START ---
You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**
You may receive a `PREVIOUS CONTEXT` field. This tells you the state of the document immediately before the current chunk.
- If the previous chunk ended inside a section (e.g., "Table of Contents"), you MUST continue that section unless a clear new header appears.
- Do NOT start a new `CLAUSE_START` if the text is clearly a continuation of a list or table from the previous section.

**Style Rules:**
- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).
- Do NOT classify TOC items as `CLAUSE_START`.

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.
    - If the text says "Schedule", use `APPENDIX_START` (unless specifically instructed otherwise, but usually Schedule = Appendix).
- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:
    - If you are inside a section (e.g., Annex) and see text that looks like a table row (e.g., "| Col 1 | Col 2 |"), tag it as `CONTENT`.
    - **Ignore Repeated Headers**: If you see headers like "Table continued", "Page X", or repeated column names inside a table, tag them as `CONTENT`. Do NOT start a new section.

**Output Format:**
Return a JSON list of objects. Each object must have:
- `index`: The EXACT integer index from the input block.
- `type`: The classification tag.

Example: `[{"index": 0, "type": "INFO"}, {"index": 1, "type": "CLAUSE"}]`

**Allowed Tags & Rules:**

If Document Type is **MASTER** or **SUBORDINATE**:
**Goal:** Group the document into high-level sections. Do NOT split sub-sections.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-contractual section.
    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the first block (header/title) of this section.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

If Document Type is **REFERENCE**:
**Goal:** Identify Guidelines.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-guideline section.
    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).

--- CHUNK START ---
You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**
You may receive a `PREVIOUS CONTEXT` field. This tells you the state of the document immediately before the current chunk.
- If the previous chunk ended inside a section (e.g., "Table of Contents"), you MUST continue that section unless a clear new header appears.
- Do NOT start a new `CLAUSE_START` if the text is clearly a continuation of a list or table from the previous section.

**Style Rules:**
- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).
- Do NOT classify TOC items as `CLAUSE_START`.

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.
    - If the text says "Schedule", use `APPENDIX_START` (unless specifically instructed otherwise, but usually Schedule = Appendix).
- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:
    - If you are inside a section (e.g., Annex) and see text that looks like a table row (e.g., "| Col 1 | Col 2 |"), tag it as `CONTENT`.
    - **Ignore Repeated Headers**: If you see headers like "Table continued", "Page X", or repeated column names inside a table, tag them as `CONTENT`. Do NOT start a new section.

**Output Format:**
Return a JSON list of objects. Each object must have:
- `index`: The EXACT integer index from the input block.
- `type`: The classification tag.

Example: `[{"index": 0, "type": "INFO"}, {"index": 1, "type": "CLAUSE"}]`

**Allowed Tags & Rules:**

If Document Type is **MASTER** or **SUBORDINATE**:
**Goal:** Group the document into high-level sections. Do NOT split sub-sections.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-contractual section.
    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the first block (header/title) of this section.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

If Document Type is **REFERENCE**:
**Goal:** Identify Guidelines.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-guideline section.
    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).

A warranty is a statement of fact made by the warrantor to the warrantee. Warranties often take the form of assurances from the seller as to the condition of the sold product or service. A product warranty is essentially a formal promise by a vendor that the product sold performs and/or has the qualities as the vendor has promised. Warranties are generally either express or implied. Express warranties are affirmative written promises about the quality and features of the products/services being sold that are specifically listed in the in the purchasing contract. For example, a battery will last 2 years under normal use.  In contract to express warranties, an implied warranty is derived from applicable legislation or trade usage and is made, regardless of whether or not it is specifically mentioned in the contract. --- CHUNK START ---
You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**
You may receive a `PREVIOUS CONTEXT` field. This tells you the state of the document immediately before the current chunk.
- If the previous chunk ended inside a section (e.g., "Table of Contents"), you MUST continue that section unless a clear new header appears.
- Do NOT start a new `CLAUSE_START` if the text is clearly a continuation of a list or table from the previous section.

**Style Rules:**
- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).
- Do NOT classify TOC items as `CLAUSE_START`.

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.
    - If the text says "Schedule", use `APPENDIX_START` (unless specifically instructed otherwise, but usually Schedule = Appendix).
- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:
    - If you are inside a section (e.g., Annex) and see text that looks like a table row (e.g., "| Col 1 | Col 2 |"), tag it as `CONTENT`.
    - **Ignore Repeated Headers**: If you see headers like "Table continued", "Page X", or repeated column names inside a table, tag them as `CONTENT`. Do NOT start a new section.

**Output Format:**
Return a JSON list of objects. Each object must have:
- `index`: The EXACT integer index from the input block.
- `type`: The classification tag.

Example: `[{"index": 0, "type": "INFO"}, {"index": 1, "type": "CLAUSE"}]`

**Allowed Tags & Rules:**

If Document Type is **MASTER** or **SUBORDINATE**:
**Goal:** Group the document into high-level sections. Do NOT split sub-sections.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-contractual section.
    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the first block (header/title) of this section.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

If Document Type is **REFERENCE**:
**Goal:** Identify Guidelines.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-guideline section.
    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).

You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**

- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.

- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:

--- CHUNK START ---
You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**
You may receive a `PREVIOUS CONTEXT` field. This tells you the state of the document immediately before the current chunk.
- If the previous chunk ended inside a section (e.g., "Table of Contents"), you MUST continue that section unless a clear new header appears.
- Do NOT start a new `CLAUSE_START` if the text is clearly a continuation of a list or table from the previous section.

**Style Rules:**
- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).
- Do NOT classify TOC items as `CLAUSE_START`.

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.
    - If the text says "Schedule", use `APPENDIX_START` (unless specifically instructed otherwise, but usually Schedule = Appendix).
- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:
    - If you are inside a section (e.g., Annex) and see text that looks like a table row (e.g., "| Col 1 | Col 2 |"), tag it as `CONTENT`.
    - **Ignore Repeated Headers**: If you see headers like "Table continued", "Page X", or repeated column names inside a table, tag them as `CONTENT`. Do NOT start a new section.

**Output Format:**
Return a JSON list of objects. Each object must have:
- `index`: The EXACT integer index from the input block.
- `type`: The classification tag.

Example: `[{"index": 0, "type": "INFO"}, {"index": 1, "type": "CLAUSE"}]`

**Allowed Tags & Rules:**

If Document Type is **MASTER** or **SUBORDINATE**:
**Goal:** Group the document into high-level sections. Do NOT split sub-sections.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-contractual section.
    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the first block (header/title) of this section.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

If Document Type is **REFERENCE**:
**Goal:** Identify Guidelines.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-guideline section.
    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).

--- CHUNK START ---
You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**
You may receive a `PREVIOUS CONTEXT` field. This tells you the state of the document immediately before the current chunk.
- If the previous chunk ended inside a section (e.g., "Table of Contents"), you MUST continue that section unless a clear new header appears.
- Do NOT start a new `CLAUSE_START` if the text is clearly a continuation of a list or table from the previous section.

**Style Rules:**
- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).
- Do NOT classify TOC items as `CLAUSE_START`.

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.
    - If the text says "Schedule", use `APPENDIX_START` (unless specifically instructed otherwise, but usually Schedule = Appendix).
- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:
    - If you are inside a section (e.g., Annex) and see text that looks like a table row (e.g., "| Col 1 | Col 2 |"), tag it as `CONTENT`.
    - **Ignore Repeated Headers**: If you see headers like "Table continued", "Page X", or repeated column names inside a table, tag them as `CONTENT`. Do NOT start a new section.

**Output Format:**
Return a JSON list of objects. Each object must have:
- `index`: The EXACT integer index from the input block.
- `type`: The classification tag.

Example: `[{"index": 0, "type": "INFO"}, {"index": 1, "type": "CLAUSE"}]`

**Allowed Tags & Rules:**

If Document Type is **MASTER** or **SUBORDINATE**:
**Goal:** Group the document into high-level sections. Do NOT split sub-sections.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-contractual section.
    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the first block (header/title) of this section.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

If Document Type is **REFERENCE**:
**Goal:** Identify Guidelines.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-guideline section.
    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).


CURRENT DOCUMENT TYPE: MASTER

1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).

--- CHUNK START ---
You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**
You may receive a `PREVIOUS CONTEXT` field. This tells you the state of the document immediately before the current chunk.
- If the previous chunk ended inside a section (e.g., "Table of Contents"), you MUST continue that section unless a clear new header appears.
- Do NOT start a new `CLAUSE_START` if the text is clearly a continuation of a list or table from the previous section.

**Style Rules:**
- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).
- Do NOT classify TOC items as `CLAUSE_START`.

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.
    - If the text says "Schedule", use `APPENDIX_START` (unless specifically instructed otherwise, but usually Schedule = Appendix).
- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:
    - If you are inside a section (e.g., Annex) and see text that looks like a table row (e.g., "| Col 1 | Col 2 |"), tag it as `CONTENT`.
    - **Ignore Repeated Headers**: If you see headers like "Table continued", "Page X", or repeated column names inside a table, tag them as `CONTENT`. Do NOT start a new section.

**Output Format:**
Return a JSON list of objects. Each object must have:
- `index`: The EXACT integer index from the input block.
- `type`: The classification tag.

Example: `[{"index": 0, "type": "INFO"}, {"index": 1, "type": "CLAUSE"}]`

**Allowed Tags & Rules:**

If Document Type is **MASTER** or **SUBORDINATE**:
**Goal:** Group the document into high-level sections. Do NOT split sub-sections.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-contractual section.
    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the first block (header/title) of this section.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

If Document Type is **REFERENCE**:
**Goal:** Identify Guidelines.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-guideline section.
    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).

--- CHUNK START ---
You are a legal document structure analyzer.
Your task is to classify text blocks from a contract into specific categories based on the document type.

**Input Format:**
You will receive a JSON list of blocks. Each block has an `index`, `text`, and optionally `style`.
Example: `[{"index": 0, "text": "1. DEFINITIONS", "style": "Heading 1"}, {"index": 1, "text": "In this agreement..."}]`

**Context Awareness:**
You may receive a `PREVIOUS CONTEXT` field. This tells you the state of the document immediately before the current chunk.
- If the previous chunk ended inside a section (e.g., "Table of Contents"), you MUST continue that section unless a clear new header appears.
- Do NOT start a new `CLAUSE_START` if the text is clearly a continuation of a list or table from the previous section.

**Style Rules:**
- If `style` contains "TOC", "Table of Contents", or "Index", classify it as `CONTENT` (or `INFO_START` if it's the main header).
- Do NOT classify TOC items as `CLAUSE_START`.

**Strict Rules:**
- **Annex vs Appendix**: Do NOT confuse them.
    - If the text says "Annex", use `ANNEX_START`.
    - If the text says "Appendix", use `APPENDIX_START`.
    - If the text says "Schedule", use `APPENDIX_START` (unless specifically instructed otherwise, but usually Schedule = Appendix).
- **Plural Headers**: Generic plural headers like "APPENDICES", "SCHEDULES", or "EXHIBITS" (without a specific letter/number) are `INFO_START`. Do NOT tag them as `APPENDIX_START`.
- **Table Continuity**:
    - If you are inside a section (e.g., Annex) and see text that looks like a table row (e.g., "| Col 1 | Col 2 |"), tag it as `CONTENT`.
    - **Ignore Repeated Headers**: If you see headers like "Table continued", "Page X", or repeated column names inside a table, tag them as `CONTENT`. Do NOT start a new section.

**Output Format:**
Return a JSON list of objects. Each object must have:
- `index`: The EXACT integer index from the input block.
- `type`: The classification tag.

Example: `[{"index": 0, "type": "INFO"}, {"index": 1, "type": "CLAUSE"}]`

**Allowed Tags & Rules:**

If Document Type is **MASTER** or **SUBORDINATE**:
**Goal:** Group the document into high-level sections. Do NOT split sub-sections.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-contractual section.
    -   Examples: Preamble, Recitals, Table of Contents, Party Details, Signature Pages.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the first block (header/title) of this section.

2.  `CLAUSE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a main contractual clause.
    -   Examples: "1. DEFINITIONS", "2. TERM", "ARTICLE 3: FEES".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the main header (e.g. "1.", "Article I"). Do NOT tag sub-headers (e.g. "1.1") with this.

3.  `APPENDIX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Appendix.
    -   Examples: "APPENDIX A", "APPENDIX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

4.  `ANNEX_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Annex.
    -   Examples: "ANNEX A", "ANNEX 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

5.  `EXHIBIT_START`: Use this for the **START** of an Exhibit.
    -   Examples: "EXHIBIT A", "EXHIBIT 1".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

6.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, sub-clauses (1.1, 1.1.1), list items, and content following a header.
    -   This content will be grouped under the preceding `_START` tag.

If Document Type is **REFERENCE**:
**Goal:** Identify Guidelines.

**Allowed Tags:**

1.  `INFO_START`: Use this for the **START** of a non-guideline section.
    -   Examples: Title, Introduction, Scope.
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

2.  `GUIDELINE_START`: Use this for the **START** of a Guideline section.
    -   Examples: "Guideline 1", "Policy A", "Standard 1.2".
    -   Rule: Tag ONLY the header.

3.  `CONTENT`: Use this for **EVERYTHING ELSE**.
    -   Body text, list items, and content following a header.

**Prohibited Tags for REFERENCE:**
-   Do NOT use `CLAUSE_START`, `APPENDIX_START`, `ANNEX_START`, or `EXHIBIT_START`.

**Critical Instructions:**
1.  **Preserve Indices**: Return a classification for EVERY block.
2.  **No IDs**: Do NOT generate `id` fields.
3.  **One Section = One Start Tag**: Do not fragment a section. For example, "1. Definitions" gets `CLAUSE_START`. "1.1" gets `CONTENT`. "1.2" gets `CONTENT`. This keeps them all in one "Clause 1" block.
4.  **Appendices**: "APPENDIX A" gets `APPENDIX_START`. All text inside it gets `CONTENT`.
5.  **Ignore References**: Do NOT use `_START` tags for mentions in a Table of Contents. Use `CONTENT` or `INFO_START` (if it's the TOC header).
